Chem. Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">231</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">240</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D49%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D231-240%26journal%3DAcc.%2BChem.%2BRes.%26author%3DW.%2BLuo%26author%3DF.%2BShen%26author%3DC.%2BBommier%26author%3DH.%2BZhu%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26author%3DL.%2BHu%26title%3DNa-Ion%2BBattery%2BAnodes%253A%2BMaterials%2Band%2BElectrochemistry%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10165&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.accounts.5b00482&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.  Furthermore, electrochem. intercalation of Na ions into reduced graphene oxide is applied for fabricating transparent conductors, demonstrating the great feasibility of Na ion intercalation for optical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGorKnQvVSK3P7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhGtQMfdOvDhg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XhtVGksrg%253D&amp;md5=90d2907a2b33fdcf59913255073dd969</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1039/c3ee40847g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.-S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Room-temperature Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries for Large-Scale Electric Energy Storage</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ. Sci.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2013</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">6</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">2338</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">2360</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/c3ee40847g</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D6%26publication_year%3D2013%26pages%3D2338-2360%26journal%3DEnergy%2BEnviron.%2BSci.%26author%3DH.%2BPan%26author%3DY.-S.%2BHu%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26title%3DRoom-temperature%2BStationary%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%2Bfor%2BLarge-Scale%2BElectric%2BEnergy%2BStorage%26doi%3D10.1039%252Fc3ee40847g&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10165&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2Fc3ee40847g&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit2R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">2</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Room-temperature stationary sodium-ion batteries for large-scale electric energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Pan, Huilin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Chen, Liquan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2338-2360</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liUgyKn46IT-Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201003587"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functional Materials for Rechargeable Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv. Mater.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2011</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">23</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1695</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1715</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/adma.201003587</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D23%26publication_year%3D2011%26pages%3D1695-1715%26journal%3DAdv.%2BMater.%26author%3DF.%2BCheng%26author%3DJ.%2BLiang%26author%3DZ.%2BTao%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26title%3DFunctional%2BMaterials%2Bfor%2BRechargeable%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fadma.201003587&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10165&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fadma.201003587&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit3R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">3</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Functional Materials for Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cheng, Fang-Yi; Liang, Jing; Tao, Zhan-Liang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2011</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">23</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review of recent progress in functional materials applied in the currently prevailing rechargeable lithium-ion, nickel-metal hydride, lead-acid, vanadium redox flow, and sodium-sulfur batteries.  The focus is on research activities toward the ionic, at., or mol. diffusion and transport; electron transfer; surface/interface structure optimization; the regulation of the electrochem. reactions; and the key materials and devices for rechargeable batteries.  Rechargeable batteries cover applications in many fields, which include portable electronic consumer devices, elec. vehicles, and large-scale electricity storage in smart or intelligent grids.  The performance of rechargeable batteries depends essentially on the thermodn. and kinetics of the electrochem. reactions involved in the components (i.e., the anode, cathode, electrolyte, and separator) of the cells.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.  The engineering modeling calcns. of Na-ion battery energy d. indicate that 210 Wh kg-1 in gravimetric energy is possible for Na-ion batteries compared to existing Li-ion technol. if a cathode capacity of 200 mAh g-1 and a 500 mAh g-1 anode can be discovered with an av. cell potential of 3.3 V.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojsFXLPEQzILVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhV-JcfuWrJUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XntlSnurc%253D&amp;md5=fa5d7d089d261a40896cb6b03e88bfbe</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee02781j"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Palomares, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Serras, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Villaluenga, I.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hueso, K.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-ion batteries, recent advances and present challenges to become low cost energy storage systems</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Palomares, Veronica; Serras, Paula; Villaluenga, Irune; Hueso, Karina B.; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Rojo, Teofilo</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoRYtxfVVW_sLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhV-JcfuWrJUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XivFWnu7s%253D&amp;md5=72869139086b8ee9adec746418ff84b1</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref8"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref8'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">8</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit8" data-doi="10.1039/c2ee22864e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Abouimrane, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Weng, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Eltayeb, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cui, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Niklas, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Poluektov, O.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Amine, K.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium Insertion in Carboxylate Based Materials and Their Application in 3.6 V Full Sodium Cells</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Energy Environ.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium insertion in carboxylate based materials and their application in 3.6 V full sodium cells</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Abouimrane, Ali; Weng, Wei; Eltayeb, Hussameldin; Cui, Yanjie; Niklas, Jens; Poluektov, Oleg; Amine, Khalil</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium battery has the potential to be the next generation rechargeable system which utilizes cheaper and more abundant sodium material but affords nearly the same power as lithium batteries.  One of the key barriers for the sodium battery is the lack of stable anode materials which can insert sodium ions reversibly at relatively low potential.  This contribution reports the sodium insertion in a series of org. carboxylate based materials: (C8H4Na2O4), (C8H6O4), (C8H5NaO4), (C8Na2F4O4), (C10H2Na4O8), (C14H4O6) and (C14H4Na4O8) at low voltage (below 0.6 V vs. Na/Na+).  These org. anode materials can insert reversibly up to 2 Na per mol. with good cycleability.  The Na insertion mechanism was proposed and 3.6 V full sodium batteries were made and cycled reversibly at room temp. and at 55 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqohlWV-41Oy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhV-JcfuWrJUg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFCjs7bE&amp;md5=9c98061a338ffda869b2748427bc4a2a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref9'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit9" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201301651"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To improve the energy/power d. of energy storage materials, numerous efforts have focused on the exploration of new structure prototypes, in particular metal-org. fameworks, Prussian blue analogs, open-framework oxides, and polyanion salts.  Here the authors report a novel pyrochlore phase that appears to be useful as a high-capacity cathode for Li and Na batteries.  It is an Fe fluoride polymorph characterized by an intersecting tunnel structure, providing the space for accommodation and transport of Li and Na ions.  It is prepd. using hydrolyzable ionic liqs., which serve as reaction educts and structure-directing agents not only as far as the chem. structure is concerned but also in terms of morphol.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium Salt of Tetrahydroxybenzoquinone: Toward the Development of a Sustainable Li-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Chen, Haiyan; Armand, Michel; Courty, Matthieu; Jiang, Meng; Grey, Clare P.; Dolhem, Franck; Tarascon, Jean-Marie; Poizot, Philippe</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The use of lithiated redox org. mols. contg. electrochem. active C=O functionalities, such as lithiated oxocarbon salts, is proposed.  These represent alternative electrode materials to those used in current Li-ion battery technol. that can be synthesized from renewable starting materials.  The key material is the tetralithium salt of tetrahydroxybenzoquinone (Li4C6O6), which can be both reduced to Li2C6O6 and oxidized to Li6C6O6.                         cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">All Organic Sodium-Ion Batteries with Na4C8H2O6</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Shiwen; Wang, Lijiang; Zhu, Zhiqiang; Hu, Zhe; Zhao, Qing; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Developing org. compds. with multifunctional groups to be used as electrode materials for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries is very important.  The org. tetrasodium salt of 2,5-dihydroxyterephthalic acid (Na4DHTPA; Na4C8H2O6), which was prepd. through a green one-pot method, was investigated at potential windows of 1.6-2.8 V as the pos. electrode or 0.1-1.8 V as the neg. electrode (vs. Na+/Na), each delivering compatible and stable capacities of ca. 180 mAh g-1 with excellent cycling.  A combination of electrochem., spectroscopic and computational studies revealed that reversible uptake/removal of two Na+ ions is assocd. with the enolate groups at 1.6-2.8 V (Na2C8H2O6/Na4C8H2O6) and the carboxylate groups at 0.1-1.8 V (Na4C8H2O6/Na6C8H2O6).                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unraveling the storage mechanism in organic carbonyl electrodes for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Xiaoyan; Jin, Shifeng; Zhang, Zhizhen; Jiang, Liwei; Mu, Linqin; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Xiaolong; Armand, Michel; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Science Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">1</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">8</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. carbonyl compds. represent a promising class of electrode materials for secondary batteries; however, the storage mechanism still remains unclear.  We take Na2C6H2O4 as an example to unravel the mechanism.  It consists of alternating Na-O octahedral inorg. layer and π-stacked benzene org. layer in spatial sepn., delivering a high reversible capacity and first coulombic efficiency.  The expt. and calcn. results reveal that the Na-O inorg. layer provides both Na+ ion transport pathway and storage site, whereas the benzene org. layer provides electron transport pathway and redox center.  Our contribution provides a brand-new insight in understanding the storage mechanism in inorg.-org. layered host and opens up a new exciting direction for designing new materials for secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvhaHOKa68pLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg329u5wbgC9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpt1OgtrY%253D&amp;md5=668f6601756b71e7ce62d0f0fb76218d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b02569"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kwon, J.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High Energy Organic Cathode for Sodium Rechargeable Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, Haegyeom; Kwon, Ji Eon; Lee, Byungju; Hong, Jihyun; Lee, Minah; Park, Soo Young; Kang, Kisuk</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. electrodes have attracted significant attention as alternatives to conventional inorg. electrodes in terms of sustainability and universal availability in natural systems.  However, low working voltages and low energy densities are inherent limitations in cathode applications.  Here, we propose a high-energy org. cathode using a quinone-deriv., C6Cl4O2, for use in sodium-ion batteries, which boasts one of the highest av. voltages among org. electrodes in sodium batteries (∼2.72 V vs Na/Na+).  It also utilizes a two-electron transfer to provide an energy of 580 Wh kg-1.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. reveal that the introduction of electroneg. elements into the quinone structure significantly increased the sodium storage potential and thus enhanced the energy d. of the electrode, the latter being substantially higher than previously known quinone-derived cathodes.  The cycle stability of C6Cl4O2 was enhanced by incorporating the C6Cl4O2 into a nanocomposite with a porous carbon template.  This prevented the dissoln. of active mols. into the surrounding electrolyte.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrDvrAslSbtB7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg329u5wbgC9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhs1Ors7fJ&amp;md5=9fcd8e7ab6212af97a06a260542e2727</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201002439"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Song, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhan, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, Y.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polyimides: Promising Energy-Storage Materials</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit15R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">15</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polyimides: promising energy-storage materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Song, Zhiping; Zhan, Hui; Zhou, Yunhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Use of polyimides as cathode materials for rechargeable lithium batteries was proposed for the first time.  Although they are regarded as insulators, the five polyimide samples are all electrochem. active; they all benefit from the good reaction reversibility of the imide group and the stable polymer framework.  The two-electron transfer of each monomer unit results in a specific discharge capacity of around 200 mAhg-1, a discharge voltage of 2.0-2.5 V, and a coulomb efficiency close to 100%.  Moreover, the intrinsic stability and insoly. of the polyimide ensures that it is not dissolved in the electrolyte, and thus allows cyclability.  Since polyimide is hydrolyzable under specified conditions, it is environmentally friendly and conforms to the requirements of a "green battery".</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1i5fPt1DiArVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg329u5wbgC9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3cXhtlGmsrjI&amp;md5=669fe050d3ed05336fbcaf88f529628f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201402402"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Castillo-Martinez, E.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Carretero-Gonzalez, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Armand, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Castillo-Martinez, Elizabeth; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Armand, Michel</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The redox entity comprising two Schiff base groups attached to a Ph ring (of structure [-N=CH-Ar-CH=N-]) is reported to be active for sodium-ion storage (Ar = arom. group).  Electroactive polymeric Schiff bases were produced by reaction between non-conjugated aliph. or conjugated arom. diamine block with terephthalaldehyde unit.  Cryst. polymeric Schiff bases are able to electrochem. store more than one sodium atom per azomethine group at potentials between 0 and 1.5 V vs. Na+/Na.  The redox potential can be tuned through conjugation of the polymeric chain and by electron injection from donor substituents in the arom. rings.  Reversible capacities of up to 350 mA h g-1 are achieved when the carbon mixt. is optimized with Ketjen Black.  Interestingly, the "reverse" configuration (of structure [-CH=N-Ar-N=CH-]) is not electrochem. active, though isoelectronic.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfY8JYZw4ZirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR883xXJuR3g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmslakur4%253D&amp;md5=53412644537ae0ee4c6334a00b670423</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601415"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wild, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Strumpf, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Häupler, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hager, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. rechargeable batteries have received significant research interest from the viewpoints of structural diversity and sustainability of electrode materials.  Core structures are designed of org. cathode materials for lithium-ion (Li-ion) batteries based on d. functional theory (DFT) calcns., which indicated that six-membered cyclic 1,2-diketones serve as excellent core structures because of the high redox energy change resulting from favorable coordination of the oxygen atoms to Li and the aromaticity of the reduced form.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible Li and Na storage behaviors of perylenetetracarboxylates as organic anodes for Li- and Na-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, R. R.; Cao, Y. L.; Ai, X. P.; Yang, H. X.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Electroanalytical Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries using org. materials have potential advantages of low cost and materials sustainability for large-scale elec. storage applications.  The key issue to realize such sustainable batteries is to develop suitable org. electrode materials with sufficient redox capacity and cycling stability.  Herein, the authors introduce Li and Na salt of 3, 4, 9,10-perylenetetracarboxylic acid (Li4C24H8O8, Na4C24H8O8) as new org. anode materials for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.  The Li4C24H8O8 electrode can deliver a reversible capacity of ∼200 mAh g-1 at quite low charge/discharge plateaus of 1.20/1.10 V, and remains 98% of its initial capacity after 100 cycles.  Similarly, the Na4C24H8O8 electrode exhibits a reversible Na storage capacity of ∼100 mAh g-1 at a low voltage region of 0.8-0.6 V (vs. Na) with almost indiscernible capacity decay during 100 cycles.  These results demonstrate a potential possibility to use the org. anodes for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo2UU3gdaA7XbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR883xXJuR3g"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is a challenge to prep. org. electrodes for sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life and high capacity.  The highly reactive radical intermediates generated during the sodiation/desodiation process could be a crit. issue because of undesired side reactions.  Here we present durable electrodes with a stabilized α-C radical intermediate.  Through the resonance effect as well as steric effects, the excessive reactivity of the unpaired electron is successfully suppressed, thus developing an electrode with stable cycling for over 2,000 cycles with 96.8% capacity retention.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Review-Advanced Carbon-Supported Organic Electrode Materials for Lithium (Sodium)-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Zhiqiang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the Electrochemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electroactive org. compds. represent one of the most promising electrode materials for the next generation of green and sustainable lithium (sodium) ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs).  However, most org. electrode materials are plagued by high soly. in org. electrolytes and poor elec. cond., which have severely impeded their practical applications.  Among various strategies to improve their electrochem. performance, introducing conductive carbon into org. materials to form composite electrodes offers the possibility to simultaneously solve the two problems.  In this paper, an overview is provided of recent development in the design, synthesis, and application of advanced carbon-supported org. electrode materials for LIBs/SIBs.  In such systems, org. component mainly contributes to the charge storage, while carbon matrix facilitates the electron transfer and suppresses the dissoln. of the active materials.  Mainly the focus is on representative composites with carbon matrix of fibers, nanotubes (CNTs), graphene, and porous structures.  The employment of CNTs and graphene as conductive carbon substrates is highlighted for org. electrode materials due to their high cond., huge surface area, and excellent flexibility.  The elegant design of org.-carbon composite should promote the practical applications of org. electrode materials for LIBs/SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqGsx2sGwY0m7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljR883xXJuR3g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslelu73M&amp;md5=3fe74ac1efb8939bdee1512c125db19f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201102372"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ohtani, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyaizu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishide, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Geckeler, K.                         cas_cit25R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">25</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Generalized gradient approximation made simple</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Burke, Kieron; Ernzerhof, Matthias</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) for the exchange-correlation energy improve upon the local spin d. (LSD) description of atoms, mols., and solids.  We present a simple derivation of a simple GGA, in which all parameters (other than those in LSD) are fundamental consts.  Only general features of the detailed construction underlying the Perdew-Wang 1991 (PW91) GGA are invoked.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Atoms, molecules, solids, and surfaces:  applications of the generalized gradient approximation for exchange and correlation</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Perdew, John P.; Chevary, J. A.; Vosko, S. H.; Jackson, Koblar A.; Pederson, Mark R.; Singh, D. J.; Fiolhais, Carlos</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B:  Condensed Matter and Materials Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1992</span>),

    </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) seek to improve upon the accuracy of the local-spin-d. (LSD) approxn. in electronic-structure calcns.  Perdew and Wang have developed a GGA based on real-space cutoff of the spurious long-range components of the second-order gradient expansion for the exchange-correlation hole.  Authors have found that this d. functional performs well in numerical tests for a variety of systems: Total energies of 30 atoms are highly accurate.  Ionization energies and electron affinities are improved in a statistical sense, although significant interconfigurational and interterm errors remain.  Accurate atomization energies are found for seven hydrocarbon mols., with a rms error per bond of 0.1 eV, compared with 0.7 eV for the LSD approxn. and 2.4 eV for the Hartree-Fock approxn.  For atoms and mols., there is a cancellation of error between d. functionals for exchange and correlation, which is most striking whenever the Hartree-Fock result is furthest from expt.  The surprising LSD underestimation of the lattice consts. of Li and Na by 3-4% is cor., and the magnetic ground state of solid Fe is restored.  The work function, surface energy (neglecting the long-range contribution), and curvature energy of a metallic surface are all slightly reduced in comparison with LSD.  Taking account of the pos. long-range contribution, authors find surface and curvature energies in good agreement with exptl. or exact values.  Finally, a way is found to visualize and understand the nonlocality of exchange and correlation, its origins, and its phys. effects.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfVQ8PrAQBWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li8BvARtYGdyA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK38XlvFyks7c%253D&amp;md5=e52b617f523b1a8c545707544ce01d05</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kresse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Furthmuller, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes for Ab Initio Total-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficient iterative schemes for ab initio total-energy calculations using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmueller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Review B: Condensed Matter</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoK9e6g4dZiorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0li8BvARtYGdyA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28Xms1Whu7Y%253D&amp;md5=9c8f6f298fe5ffe37c2589d3f970a697</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref28'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit28" data-doi="10.1016/0927-0256(96)00008-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kresse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Furthmuller, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficiency of Ab-Initio Total Energy Calculations for Metals and Semiconductors Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Comput.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Efficiency of ab-initio total energy calculations for metals and semiconductors using a plane-wave basis set</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kresse, G.; Furthmuller, J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Computational Materials Science</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present a detailed description and comparison of algorithms for performing ab-initio quantum-mech. calcns. using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  The authors will discuss: (a) partial occupancies within the framework of the linear tetrahedron method and the finite temp. d.-functional theory, (b) iterative methods for the diagonalization of the Kohn-Sham Hamiltonian and a discussion of an efficient iterative method based on the ideas of Pulay's residual minimization, which is close to an order N2atoms scaling even for relatively large systems, (c) efficient Broyden-like and Pulay-like mixing methods for the charge d. including a new special preconditioning optimized for a plane-wave basis set, (d) conjugate gradient methods for minimizing the electronic free energy with respect to all degrees of freedom simultaneously.  The authors have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VAMP (Vienna ab-initio mol.-dynamics package).                         cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Helium dimer dispersion forces and correlation potentials in density functional theory</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Allen, Mark J.; Tozer, David J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2002</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">117</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11113-11120</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCPSA6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9606</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The dispersion interaction in the helium dimer is considered from the viewpoint of the force on a nucleus.  At large internuclear sepns., Brueckner coupled cluster BD(T) forces agree well with near-exact dispersion forces.  The at. d. distortion assocd. with the dispersion force is quantified by comparing the BD(T) dimer d. with a superposition of at. densities.  For d. functional theory calcns. in the Hartree-Fock-Kohn-Sham (HFKS) formalism, the accuracy of the dispersion force is governed by the correlation potential.  Calcns. using the conventional Lee-Yang-Parr [Phys. Rev. B 37, 785 (1988)] potential only generate a small d. distortion, giving forces significantly smaller than BD(T).  The BD(T) electron densities are therefore used to det. improved correlation potentials using a modified Zhao-Morrison-Parr (ZMP) approach [Phys. Rev. A 50, 2138 (1994)].  HFKS calcns. using these ZMP potentials quant. reproduce the distortion, giving dispersion forces in good agreement with BD(T).  The dimer ZMP correlation potential is partitioned into two parts, one equal to the sum of two unperturbed spherical at. correlation potentials and the other representing an interaction potential.  HFKS calcns. using the former do not generate the distortion; forces are close to Hartree-Fock.  Calcns. using the latter do generate the distortion, giving forces essentially identical to those from the full dimer potential.  The origin of the distortion is traced to the asym. structure of the interaction correlation potential in the vicinity of each nucleus.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqjqXKN99fNrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlBgQIoQjtbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD38XpsFKru7k%253D&amp;md5=e471f2991f13deb21b071b6ec41824d9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/jcc.540161102"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hobza, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sponer, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Reschel, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Density Functional Theory and Molecular Clusters</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1995</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1315-25</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">D. functional theory (DFT) methods, including nonlocal d. gradient terms in the exchange and correlation energy functionals, were applied to various types of mol. clusters: H-bonded, ionic, electrostatic, and London.  Reliable results on the structure and stabilization energy were obtained for the first two types of cluster as long as Becke3LYP and Becke3P86 functionals and basis sets of at least DZ + P quality were used.  DFT methods with currently available functionals failed completely, however, for London-type clusters, for which no min. was found on the potential energy surfaces.  DFT interaction energy exhibits the same basis set extension dependence as the Hartree-Fock (HF) interaction energy.  Therefore, the Boys-Bernardi function counterpoise procedure should be employed for elimination of the DFT basis set superposition error.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqwD9kF41AgbrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlBgQIoQjtbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2MXovVKqtro%253D&amp;md5=b7e9f4015c2f4cd639e8f745cccef159</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref31'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit31" data-doi="10.1016/0009-2614(94)01027-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kristyan, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pulay, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Can (Semi)Local Density-Functional Theory Account for the London Dispersion Forces</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. Phys. Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1994</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">229</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">175</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">180</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0009-2614(94)01027-7</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D229%26publication_year%3D1994%26pages%3D175-180%26journal%3DChem.%2BPhys.%2BLett.%26author%3DS.%2BKristyan%26author%3DP.%2BPulay%26title%3DCan%2B%2528Semi%2529Local%2BDensity-Functional%2BTheory%2BAccount%2Bfor%2Bthe%2BLondon%2BDispersion%2BForces%26doi%3D10.1016%252F0009-2614%252894%252901027-7&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10165&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2F0009-2614%2894%2901027-7&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1002/jcc.20495"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Grimme, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Semiempirical GGA-Type Density Functional Constructed with a Long-Range Dispersion Correction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Comput. Chem.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2006</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">27</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1787</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">99</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.20495</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D27%26publication_year%3D2006%26pages%3D1787-99%26journal%3DJ.%2BComput.%2BChem.%26author%3DS.%2BGrimme%26title%3DSemiempirical%2BGGA-Type%2BDensity%2BFunctional%2BConstructed%2Bwith%2Ba%2BLong-Range%2BDispersion%2BCorrection%26doi%3D10.1002%252Fjcc.20495&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10165&amp;doiOfLink=10.1002%2Fjcc.20495&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Semiempirical GGA-type density functional constructed with a long-range dispersion correction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grimme, Stefan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1787-1799</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new d. functional (DF) of the generalized gradient approxn. (GGA) type for general chem. applications termed B97-D is proposed.  It is based on Becke's power-series ansatz from 1997 and is explicitly parameterized by including damped atom-pairwise dispersion corrections of the form C6·R-6.  A general computational scheme for the parameters used in this correction has been established and parameters for elements up to xenon and a scaling factor for the dispersion part for several common d. functionals (BLYP, PBE, TPSS, B3LYP) are reported.  The new functional is tested in comparison with other GGAs and the B3LYP hybrid functional on std. thermochem. benchmark sets, for 40 noncovalently bound complexes, including large stacked arom. mols. and group II element clusters, and for the computation of mol. geometries.  Further cross-validation tests were performed for organometallic reactions and other difficult problems for std. functionals.  In summary, it is found that B97-D belongs to one of the most accurate general purpose GGAs, reaching, for example for the G97/2 set of heat of formations, a mean abs. deviation of only 3.8 kcal mol-1.  The performance for noncovalently bound systems including many pure van der Waals complexes is exceptionally good, reaching on the av. CCSD(T) accuracy.  The basic strategy in the development to restrict the d. functional description to shorter electron correlation lengths scales and to describe situations with medium to large interat. distances by damped C6·R-6 terms seems to be very successful, as demonstrated for some notoriously difficult reactions.  As an example, for the isomerization of larger branched to linear alkanes, B97-D is the only DF available that yields the right sign for the energy difference.  From a practical point of view, the new functional seems to be quite robust and it is thus suggested as an efficient and accurate quantum chem. method for large systems where dispersion forces are of general importance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodrkmrBLRzxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlBgQIoQjtbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XhtFenu7bO&amp;md5=0b4aa16bebc3a0a2ec175d4b161ab0e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1021/jp5056792"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">First-Principles Study of an Ethoxycarbonyl-Based Organic Electrode Material of Lithium Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Grimme, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Accurate Modeling of Organic Molecular Crystals by Dispersion-Corrected Density Functional Tight Binding (DFTB)</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Accurate Modeling of Organic Molecular Crystals by Dispersion-Corrected Density Functional Tight Binding (DFTB)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brandenburg, Jan Gerit; Grimme, Stefan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1785-1789</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCLCD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1948-7185</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ambitious goal of org. crystal structure prediction challenges theor. methods regarding their accuracy and efficiency.  Dispersion-cor. d. functional theory (DFT-D) in principle is applicable, but the computational demands, for example, to compute a huge no. of polymorphs, are too high.  Here, we demonstrate that this task can be carried out by a dispersion-cor. d. functional tight binding (DFTB) method.  The semiempirical Hamiltonian with the D3 correction can accurately and efficiently model both solid- and gas-phase inter- and intramol. interactions at a speed up of 2 orders of magnitude compared to DFT-D.  The mean abs. deviations for interaction (lattice) energies for various databases are typically 2-3 kcal/mol (10-20%), i.e., only about two times larger than those for DFT-D.  For zero-point phonon energies, small deviations of &lt;0.5 kcal/mol compared to DFT-D are obtained.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpgV0qe2TF1pbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlBgQIoQjtbg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXnsVegsbk%253D&amp;md5=7c4e54ca1b8d5ed35fba996028a06f58</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1016/0022-0248(80)90132-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rinaudo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Boistelle, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Occurence of Uric Acids and the Growth Morphology of the Anhydrous Monoclinic Modification C<sub>5</sub>H<sub>4</sub>N<sub>4</sub>O<sub>3</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The occurrence of uric acids and the growth morphology of the anhydrous monoclinic modification:  C5H4N4O3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rinaudo, C.; Boistelle, R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Crystal Growth</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1980</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>

                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCRGAE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-0248</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Anhyd. and hydrated uric acid crystals which frequently occur in human urolithiasis were grown from pure aq. solns. at 25 and 37°.  The appearance domain of either modification is given as a function of initial uric acid concn. at pH values ranging from 3.0 to 5.5.  The exptl. and theor. growth morphologies of the anhyd. phase are in agreement, the crystals exhiibiting the 〈100〉, 〈210〉, 〈121〉, 〈001〉, and 〈201〉 forms.  Crystal habit depends on supersatn.; 〈100〉 has always the largest extension at low supersatn. and 〈121〉 developes to the detriment of 〈210〉, 〈001〉, and 〈201〉.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQe4vYiU498bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljlBgQIoQjtbg"> &gt;&gt;         </p><ol id="rightTab-references" class="useLabel"><li id="rightTab-ref1"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref1" class="rightTabRefNumLink">1</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit1" data-doi="10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Shen, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Acc. Chem. Res.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">231</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">240</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.accounts.5b00482</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit1R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">1</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na-Ion Battery Anodes: Materials and Electrochemistry</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Wei; Shen, Fei; Bommier, Clement; Zhu, Hongli; Ji, Xiulei; Hu, Liangbing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Accounts of Chemical Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">2</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">231-240</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACHRE4</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0001-4842</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The intermittent nature of renewable energy sources, such as solar and wind, calls for sustainable elec. energy storage (EES) technologies for stationary applications.  Li will be simply too rare for Li-ion batteries (LIBs) to be used for large-scale storage purposes.  In contrast, Na-ion batteries (NIBs) are highly promising to meet the demand of grid-level storage because Na is truly earth abundant and ubiquitous around the globe.  Furthermore, NIBs share a similar rocking-chair operation mechanism with LIBs, which potentially provides high reversibility and long cycling life.  It would be most efficient to transfer knowledge learned on LIBs during the last three decades to the development of NIBs.  Following this logic, rapid progress has been made in NIB cathode materials, where layered metal oxides and polyanionic compds. exhibit encouraging results.  On the anode side, pure graphite as the std. anode for LIBs can only form NaC64 in NIBs if solvent co-intercalation does not occur due to the unfavorable thermodn.  In fact, it was the utilization of a carbon anode in LIBs that enabled the com. successes.  Anodes of metal-ion batteries det. key characteristics, such as safety and cycling life; thus, it is indispensable to identify suitable anode materials for NIBs.In this Account, we review recent development on anode materials for NIBs.  Due to the limited space, we will mainly discuss carbon-based and alloy-based anodes and highlight progress made in our groups in this field.  We first present what is known about the failure mechanism of graphite anode in NIBs.  We then go on to discuss studies on hard carbon anodes, alloy-type anodes, and org. anodes.  Esp., the multiple functions of natural cellulose that is used as a low-cost carbon precursor for mass prodn. and as a soft substrate for tin anodes are highlighted.  The strategies of minimizing the surface area of carbon anodes for improving the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency are also outlined, where graphene oxide was employed as dehydration agent and 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) was used to unzip wood fiber.  Furthermore, surface modification by at. layer deposition technol. is introduced, where we discover that a thin layer of Al2O3 can function to encapsulate Sn nanoparticles, leading to a much enhanced cycling performance.  We also highlight recent work about the phosphorene/graphene anode, which outperformed other anodes in terms of capacity.  The arom. org. anode is also studied as anode with very high initial sodiation capacity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.  However, after intensive research efforts, we believe that low-cost, long-life and room-temp. sodium-ion batteries would be promising for applications in large-scale energy storage system in the near future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpqNKJTie6WmbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgBJjJmX62WAw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhtFOisrzJ&amp;md5=2e02460553edc21e1ea8b73982ed63bb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref3"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref3" class="rightTabRefNumLink">3</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit3" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201003587"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liang, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Functional Materials for Rechargeable Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  The status of ambient temp. sodium ion batteries is reviewed in light of recent developments in anode, electrolyte and cathode materials.  These devices, although early in their stage of development, are promising for large-scale grid storage applications due to the abundance and very low cost of sodium-contg. precursors used to make the components.  The engineering knowledge developed recently for highly successful Li ion batteries can be leveraged to ensure rapid progress in this area, although different electrode materials and electrolytes will be required for dual intercalation systems based on sodium.  In particular, new anode materials need to be identified, since the graphite anode, commonly used in lithium systems, does not intercalate sodium to any appreciable extent.  A wider array of choices is available for cathodes, including high performance layered transition metal oxides and polyanionic compds.  Recent developments in electrodes are encouraging, but a great deal of research is necessary, particularly in new electrolytes, and the understanding of the SEI films.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The sodium battery has the potential to be the next generation rechargeable system which utilizes cheaper and more abundant sodium material but affords nearly the same power as lithium batteries.  One of the key barriers for the sodium battery is the lack of stable anode materials which can insert sodium ions reversibly at relatively low potential.  This contribution reports the sodium insertion in a series of org. carboxylate based materials: (C8H4Na2O4), (C8H6O4), (C8H5NaO4), (C8Na2F4O4), (C10H2Na4O8), (C14H4O6) and (C14H4Na4O8) at low voltage (below 0.6 V vs. Na/Na+).  These org. anode materials can insert reversibly up to 2 Na per mol. with good cycleability.  The Na insertion mechanism was proposed and 3.6 V full sodium batteries were made and cycled reversibly at room temp. and at 55 °C.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqohlWV-41Oy7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljHidwmj9hmsg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC38XhsFCjs7bE&amp;md5=9c98061a338ffda869b2748427bc4a2a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref9"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref9" class="rightTabRefNumLink">9</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit9" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201301651"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, H.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. carbonyl compds. represent a promising class of electrode materials for secondary batteries; however, the storage mechanism still remains unclear.  We take Na2C6H2O4 as an example to unravel the mechanism.  It consists of alternating Na-O octahedral inorg. layer and π-stacked benzene org. layer in spatial sepn., delivering a high reversible capacity and first coulombic efficiency.  The expt. and calcn. results reveal that the Na-O inorg. layer provides both Na+ ion transport pathway and storage site, whereas the benzene org. layer provides electron transport pathway and redox center.  Our contribution provides a brand-new insight in understanding the storage mechanism in inorg.-org. layered host and opens up a new exciting direction for designing new materials for secondary batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrvhaHOKa68pLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lh5lVXIj_qezg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xpt1OgtrY%253D&amp;md5=668f6601756b71e7ce62d0f0fb76218d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.5b02569"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kim, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kwon, J.
