        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. electrodes have attracted significant attention as alternatives to conventional inorg. electrodes in terms of sustainability and universal availability in natural systems.  However, low working voltages and low energy densities are inherent limitations in cathode applications.  Here, we propose a high-energy org. cathode using a quinone-deriv., C6Cl4O2, for use in sodium-ion batteries, which boasts one of the highest av. voltages among org. electrodes in sodium batteries (∼2.72 V vs Na/Na+).  It also utilizes a two-electron transfer to provide an energy of 580 Wh kg-1.  D. functional theory (DFT) calcns. reveal that the introduction of electroneg. elements into the quinone structure significantly increased the sodium storage potential and thus enhanced the energy d. of the electrode, the latter being substantially higher than previously known quinone-derived cathodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Use of polyimides as cathode materials for rechargeable lithium batteries was proposed for the first time.  Although they are regarded as insulators, the five polyimide samples are all electrochem. active; they all benefit from the good reaction reversibility of the imide group and the stable polymer framework.  The two-electron transfer of each monomer unit results in a specific discharge capacity of around 200 mAhg-1, a discharge voltage of 2.0-2.5 V, and a coulomb efficiency close to 100%.  Moreover, the intrinsic stability and insoly. of the polyimide ensures that it is not dissolved in the electrolyte, and thus allows cyclability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The redox entity comprising two Schiff base groups attached to a Ph ring (of structure [-N=CH-Ar-CH=N-]) is reported to be active for sodium-ion storage (Ar = arom. group).  Electroactive polymeric Schiff bases were produced by reaction between non-conjugated aliph. or conjugated arom. diamine block with terephthalaldehyde unit.  Cryst. polymeric Schiff bases are able to electrochem. store more than one sodium atom per azomethine group at potentials between 0 and 1.5 V vs. Na+/Na. Reversible capacities of up to 350 mA h g-1 are achieved when the carbon mixt. is optimized with Ketjen Black.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries using org. materials have potential advantages of low cost and materials sustainability for large-scale elec. storage applications.  The key issue to realize such sustainable batteries is to develop suitable org. electrode materials with sufficient redox capacity and cycling stability.  Herein, the authors introduce Li and Na salt of 3, 4, 9,10-perylenetetracarboxylic acid (Li4C24H8O8, Na4C24H8O8) as new org. anode materials for Li-ion and Na-ion batteries.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is a challenge to prep. org. electrodes for sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life and high capacity.  The highly reactive radical intermediates generated during the sodiation/desodiation process could be a crit. issue because of undesired side reactions.  Here we present durable electrodes with a stabilized α-C radical intermediate.  Through the resonance effect as well as steric effects, the excessive reactivity of the unpaired electron is successfully suppressed, thus developing an electrode with stable cycling for over 2,000 cycles with 96.8% capacity retention.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Electroactive org. compds. represent one of the most promising electrode materials for the next generation of green and sustainable lithium (sodium) ion batteries (LIBs/SIBs).  However, most org. electrode materials are plagued by high soly. in org. electrolytes and poor elec. cond., which have severely impeded their practical applications.  Among various strategies to improve their electrochem. performance, introducing conductive carbon into org. materials to form composite electrodes offers the possibility to simultaneously solve the two problems.  In this paper, an overview is provided of recent development in the design, synthesis, and application of advanced carbon-supported org. electrode materials for LIBs/SIBs.  In such systems, org. component mainly contributes to the charge storage, while carbon matrix facilitates the electron transfer and suppresses the dissoln. of the active materials.  Mainly the focus is on representative composites with carbon matrix of fibers, nanotubes (CNTs), graphene, and porous structures.  The employment of CNTs and graphene as conductive carbon substrates is highlighted for org. electrode materials due to their high cond., huge surface area, and excellent flexibility.  The elegant design of org.-carbon composite should promote the practical applications of org. electrode materials for LIBs/SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqGsx2sGwY0m7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPTeikPuCP9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhslelu73M&amp;md5=3fe74ac1efb8939bdee1512c125db19f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref24" class="rightTabRefNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit24" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201102372"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ohtani, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Oyaizu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nishide, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Geckeler, K.     </div><div class="casAbstract">Generalized gradient approxns. (GGA's) seek to improve upon the accuracy of the local-spin-d. (LSD) approxn. in electronic-structure calcns.  Perdew and Wang have developed a GGA based on real-space cutoff of the spurious long-range components of the second-order gradient expansion for the exchange-correlation hole.  Authors have found that this d. functional performs well in numerical tests for a variety of systems: Total energies of 30 atoms are highly accurate.  Ionization energies and electron affinities are improved in a statistical sense, although significant interconfigurational and interterm errors remain.  Accurate atomization energies are found for seven hydrocarbon mols., with a rms error per bond of 0.1 eV, compared with 0.7 eV for the LSD approxn. and 2.4 eV for the Hartree-Fock approxn.  For atoms and mols., there is a cancellation of error between d. functionals for exchange and correlation, which is most striking whenever the Hartree-Fock result is furthest from expt.  The surprising LSD underestimation of the lattice consts. of Li and Na by 3-4% is cor., and the magnetic ground state of solid Fe is restored.  The work function, surface energy (neglecting the long-range contribution), and curvature energy of a metallic surface are all slightly reduced in comparison with LSD.  Taking account of the pos. long-range contribution, authors find surface and curvature energies in good agreement with exptl. or exact values.  Finally, a way is found to visualize and understand the nonlocality of exchange and correlation, its origins, and its phys. effects.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfVQ8PrAQBWrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPTeikPuCP9Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK38XlvFyks7c%253D&amp;md5=e52b617f523b1a8c545707544ce01d05</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kresse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Furthmuller, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes for Ab Initio Total-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Phys.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoK9e6g4dZiorVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK28Xms1Whu7Y%253D&amp;md5=9c8f6f298fe5ffe37c2589d3f970a697</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1016/0927-0256(96)00008-0"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kresse, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Furthmuller, J.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficiency of Ab-Initio Total Energy Calculations for Metals and Semiconductors Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Comput.                         rightTab-cas_cit29R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">29</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Helium dimer dispersion forces and correlation potentials in density functional theory</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Allen, Mark J.; Tozer, David J.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2002</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">117</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">11113-11120</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCPSA6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The dispersion interaction in the helium dimer is considered from the viewpoint of the force on a nucleus.  At large internuclear sepns., Brueckner coupled cluster BD(T) forces agree well with near-exact dispersion forces.  The at. d. distortion assocd. with the dispersion force is quantified by comparing the BD(T) dimer d. with a superposition of at. densities.  For d. functional theory calcns. in the Hartree-Fock-Kohn-Sham (HFKS) formalism, the accuracy of the dispersion force is governed by the correlation potential.  Calcns. using the conventional Lee-Yang-Parr [Phys. Rev. B 37, 785 (1988)] potential only generate a small d. distortion, giving forces significantly smaller than BD(T).  The BD(T) electron densities are therefore used to det. improved correlation potentials using a modified Zhao-Morrison-Parr (ZMP) approach [Phys. Rev. A 50, 2138 (1994)].  HFKS calcns. using these ZMP potentials quant. reproduce the distortion, giving dispersion forces in good agreement with BD(T).  The dimer ZMP correlation potential is partitioned into two parts, one equal to the sum of two unperturbed spherical at. correlation potentials and the other representing an interaction potential.  HFKS calcns. using the former do not generate the distortion; forces are close to Hartree-Fock.  Calcns. using the latter do generate the distortion, giving forces essentially identical to those from the full dimer potential.  The origin of the distortion is traced to the asym. structure of the interaction correlation potential in the vicinity of each nucleus.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrqjqXKN99fNrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD38XpsFKru7k%253D&amp;md5=e471f2991f13deb21b071b6ec41824d9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref30" class="rightTabRefNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit30" data-doi="10.1002/jcc.540161102"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hobza, P.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sponer, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Reschel, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Density Functional Theory and Molecular Clusters</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Comput. Chem.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1995</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">16</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1315</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1325</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.540161102</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Density functional theory and molecular clusters</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hobza, Pavel; Sponer, Jiri; Reschel, Tomas</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1995</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1315-25</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">D. functional theory (DFT) methods, including nonlocal d. gradient terms in the exchange and correlation energy functionals, were applied to various types of mol. clusters: H-bonded, ionic, electrostatic, and London.  Reliable results on the structure and stabilization energy were obtained for the first two types of cluster as long as Becke3LYP and Becke3P86 functionals and basis sets of at least DZ + P quality were used.  DFT methods with currently available functionals failed completely, however, for London-type clusters, for which no min. was found on the potential energy surfaces.  DFT interaction energy exhibits the same basis set extension dependence as the Hartree-Fock (HF) interaction energy.  Therefore, the Boys-Bernardi function counterpoise procedure should be employed for elimination of the DFT basis set superposition error.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqwD9kF41AgbrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaK2MXovVKqtro%253D&amp;md5=b7e9f4015c2f4cd639e8f745cccef159</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref31"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref31" class="rightTabRefNumLink">31</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit31" data-doi="10.1016/0009-2614(94)01027-7"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Kristyan, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pulay, P.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Can (Semi)Local Density-Functional Theory Account for the London Dispersion Forces</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Chem. Phys. Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1994</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">229</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">175</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">180</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0009-2614(94)01027-7</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref32" class="rightTabRefNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit32" data-doi="10.1002/jcc.20495"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Grimme, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Semiempirical GGA-Type Density Functional Constructed with a Long-Range Dispersion Correction</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Comput. Chem.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2006</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">27</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1787</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">99</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1002/jcc.20495</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Semiempirical GGA-type density functional constructed with a long-range dispersion correction</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grimme, Stefan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Computational Chemistry</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2006</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">27</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1787-1799</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCCHDD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0192-8651</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">John Wiley &amp; Sons, Inc.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new d. functional (DF) of the generalized gradient approxn. (GGA) type for general chem. applications termed B97-D is proposed.  It is based on Becke's power-series ansatz from 1997 and is explicitly parameterized by including damped atom-pairwise dispersion corrections of the form C6·R-6.  A general computational scheme for the parameters used in this correction has been established and parameters for elements up to xenon and a scaling factor for the dispersion part for several common d. functionals (BLYP, PBE, TPSS, B3LYP) are reported.  The new functional is tested in comparison with other GGAs and the B3LYP hybrid functional on std. thermochem. benchmark sets, for 40 noncovalently bound complexes, including large stacked arom. mols. and group II element clusters, and for the computation of mol. geometries.  Further cross-validation tests were performed for organometallic reactions and other difficult problems for std. functionals.  In summary, it is found that B97-D belongs to one of the most accurate general purpose GGAs, reaching, for example for the G97/2 set of heat of formations, a mean abs. deviation of only 3.8 kcal mol-1.  The performance for noncovalently bound systems including many pure van der Waals complexes is exceptionally good, reaching on the av. CCSD(T) accuracy.  The basic strategy in the development to restrict the d. functional description to shorter electron correlation lengths scales and to describe situations with medium to large interat. distances by damped C6·R-6 terms seems to be very successful, as demonstrated for some notoriously difficult reactions.  As an example, for the isomerization of larger branched to linear alkanes, B97-D is the only DF available that yields the right sign for the energy difference.  From a practical point of view, the new functional seems to be quite robust and it is thus suggested as an efficient and accurate quantum chem. method for large systems where dispersion forces are of general importance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGodrkmrBLRzxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD28XhtFenu7bO&amp;md5=0b4aa16bebc3a0a2ec175d4b161ab0e4</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1021/jp5056792"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">First-Principles Study of an Ethoxycarbonyl-Based Organic Electrode Material of Lithium Battery</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys. Chem. C</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">118</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">21813</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">21818</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jp5056792</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord empty" id="
                            rightTab-cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref34" class="rightTabRefNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit34" data-doi="10.1021/jz500755u"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Brandenburg, J. G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Grimme, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Accurate Modeling of Organic Molecular Crystals by Dispersion-Corrected Density Functional Tight Binding (DFTB)</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Phys. Chem. Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">1785</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">1789</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jz500755u</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Accurate Modeling of Organic Molecular Crystals by Dispersion-Corrected Density Functional Tight Binding (DFTB)</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Brandenburg, Jan Gerit; Grimme, Stefan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1785-1789</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPCLCD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1948-7185</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The ambitious goal of org. crystal structure prediction challenges theor. methods regarding their accuracy and efficiency.  Dispersion-cor. d. functional theory (DFT-D) in principle is applicable, but the computational demands, for example, to compute a huge no. of polymorphs, are too high.  Here, we demonstrate that this task can be carried out by a dispersion-cor. d. functional tight binding (DFTB) method.  The semiempirical Hamiltonian with the D3 correction can accurately and efficiently model both solid- and gas-phase inter- and intramol. interactions at a speed up of 2 orders of magnitude compared to DFT-D.  The mean abs. deviations for interaction (lattice) energies for various databases are typically 2-3 kcal/mol (10-20%), i.e., only about two times larger than those for DFT-D.  For zero-point phonon energies, small deviations of &lt;0.5 kcal/mol compared to DFT-D are obtained.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpgV0qe2TF1pbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXnsVegsbk%253D&amp;md5=7c4e54ca1b8d5ed35fba996028a06f58</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref35" class="rightTabRefNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit35" data-doi="10.1016/0022-0248(80)90132-3"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rinaudo, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Boistelle, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">The Occurence of Uric Acids and the Growth Morphology of the Anhydrous Monoclinic Modification C<sub>5</sub>H<sub>4</sub>N<sub>4</sub>O<sub>3</sub></span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J. Cryst. Growth</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">1980</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">49</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">569</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">579</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1016/0022-0248(80)90132-3</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">The occurrence of uric acids and the growth morphology of the anhydrous monoclinic modification:  C5H4N4O3</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rinaudo, C.; Boistelle, R.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Crystal Growth</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">1980</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">49</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">569-79</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCRGAE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0022-0248</span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Anhyd. and hydrated uric acid crystals which frequently occur in human urolithiasis were grown from pure aq. solns. at 25 and 37°.  The appearance domain of either modification is given as a function of initial uric acid concn. at pH values ranging from 3.0 to 5.5.  The exptl. and theor. growth morphologies of the anhyd. phase are in agreement, the crystals exhiibiting the 〈100〉, 〈210〉, 〈121〉, 〈001〉, and 〈201〉 forms.  Crystal habit depends on supersatn.; 〈100〉 has always the largest extension at low supersatn. and 〈121〉 developes to the detriment of 〈210〉, 〈001〉, and 〈201〉.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqQe4vYiU498bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljY4feuwsRtgA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADyaL3cXkvVGgsbY%253D&amp;md5=2939760d1f8011d21f1e6f934f631b7b</span></div></div></div></div></li></ol></li><li id="pane-m3" aria-labelledby="pane-m3" class="tab__pane tab__pane-suppInfo"><h2 class="supp-info-label">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article_supporting-info" id="rightTab-notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="rightTab-_i9">Supporting Information</h2></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b10165" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b10165</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">XRD patterns, FTIR spectra, SEM images, TEM images, and the additional electrochemical performance of UA (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10165/suppl_file/am7b10165_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10165/suppl_file/am7b10165_si_001.pdf">am7b10165_si_001.pdf (3.75 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div><div id="rightTab-figshare-widget"></div><br><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzoneRight"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="b84e6b6c-b4d0-4427-b286-3cf14d52d013" class="mb-4">

            <li>
                <a title="Abstract" class="article__jump__link internalNav" href="#Abstract" data-id="article_stickyheader_JumpTo_Abstract">
                   <span>Abstract</span>
                </a>
            </li>
            <li>
                <a title="Introduction" class="article__jump__link internalNav" href="#_i1" data-id="article_stickyheader_JumpTo_Introduction">
                   <span>Introduction</span>
                </a>

        <script nonce="90da8e4f5d2cb325-SJC">
(function(){
	
	/*Event Tracking for RIS menu dropdown - Article pages*/

	$('.cit-download-dropdown_button').on('click',function(e)
	{	
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':'Main'});

	});


	$('.cit-download-dropdown_content ul li').on('click',function(e)
	{	
	//	e.preventDefault();
	    var idx = $(this).index();
	    
	    var label = '';
	    if (idx === 0 ) {
	    	label = 'Citation';
	    } else if (idx === 1 ) {
	    	label = 'Abstract';
	    } else if (idx === 2 ) {
	    	label = 'Reference';
	    } else if (idx === 3 ) {
	    	label = 'More Options';
	    }
	   
	   gtag('event', 'Export', { 'event_category': 'Citation', 'event_label':label});
	});

	$('.header_contnav-next a').on('click', function(e){
        e.preventDefault();
        gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Right Arrow'});
	}); 

 	$('.header_contnav-pre a').on('click', function(e){
	    e.preventDefault();
	     gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Left Arrow'});
	}); 

	$('.share_button').on('click', function(e){
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Top', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Share'});
	});

	$("#pane-m1con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Figures'});
	});

	$("#pane-m2con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
	    gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'References'});
	});

	$("#pane-m3con").on('click', function(e) {
		e.preventDefault();
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Supporting Info'});
	});

	$('.tab__close').on('click', function(){
		gtag('event', 'Sidebar', { 'event_category': 'Article', 'event_label':'Close'});
	}); 



})();

</script>

<script nonce="90da8e4f5d2cb325-SJC">
    document.addEventListener("DOMContentLoaded", function(){
    // Function to get a Human readable formatted date
    function getFormattedDateForMaintenance() {
        let today = new Date();
        let dd = String(today.getDate()).padStart(2, '0');
        //January is 0
        let mm = String(today.getMonth() + 1).padStart(2, '0'); 
        let yyyy = today.getFullYear();
        
        let daysOfWeek = ['Sunday', 'Monday', 'Tuesday', 'Wednesday', 'Thursday', 'Friday', 'Saturday'];
        let monthsOfYear = ['January', 'February', 'March', 'April', 'May', 'June', 'July', 'August', 'September', 'October', 'November', 'December'];

        let dayOfWeek = daysOfWeek[today.getDay()];
        let monthOfYear = monthsOfYear[today.getMonth()];

        return dayOfWeek + ', ' + monthOfYear + ' ' + dd + ', ' + yyyy;
    }
    
    // Insert the date into the .system-message-date element
    document.querySelector('.system-message-date').innerText = getFormattedDateForMaintenance();
});
</script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90da8e4f5d2cb325-SJC">
"use strict"
//Script checks gdpr cookie and submits form
	/* 
	Create an in-page pop-up message, only for the InfoCentral homepage, that will gather email registrants for the library marketing list.
	 
	Needs the end point
	*/

var infoCentralCapture = (function() {

    //Detect mobile device
    window.mobilecheck = function() {
        var check = false;
        (function(a){if(/(android|bb\d+|meego).+mobile|avantgo|bada\/|blackberry|blazer|compal|elaine|fennec|hiptop|iemobile|ip(hone|od)|iris|kindle|lge |maemo|midp|mmp|mobile.+firefox|netfront|opera u|g560|gene|gf\-5|g\-mo|go(\.w|od)|gr(ad|un)|haie|hcit|hd\-(m|p|t)|hei\-|hi(pt|ta)|hp( i|ip)|hs\-c|ht(c(\-| |_|a|g|p|s|t)|tp)|hu(aw|tc)|i\-(20|go|ma)|i230|iac( |\-|\/)|ibro|idea|ig01|ikom|im1k|inno|ipaq|iris|ja(t|v)a|jbro|jemu|jigs|kddi|keji|kgt( |\/)|klon|kpt |kwc\-|kyo(c|k)|le(no|xi)|lg( g|\/(k|l|u)|50|54|\-[a-w])|libw|lynx|m1\-w|m3ga|m50\/|ma(te|ui|xo)|mc(01|21|ca)|m\-cr|me(rc|ri)|mi(o8|oa|ts)|mmef|mo(01|02|bi|de|do|t(\-| |o|v)|zz)|mt(50|p1|v )|mwbp|mywa|n10[0-2]|n20[2-3]|n30(0|2)|n50(0|2|5)|n7(0(0|1)|10)|ne((c|m)\-|on|tf|wf|wg|wt)|nok(6|i)|nzph|o2im|op(ti|wv)|oran|owg1|p800|pan(a|d|t)|pdxg|pg(13|\-([1-8]|c))|phil|pire|pl(ay|uc)|pn\-2|po(ck|rt|se)|prox|psio|pt\-g|qa\-a|qc(07|12|21|32|60|\-[2-7]|i\-)|qtek|r380|r600|raks|rim9|ro(ve|zo)|s55\/|sa(ge|ma|mm|ms|ny|va)|sc(01|h\-|oo|p\-)|sdk\/|se(c(\-|0|1)|47|mc|nd|ri)|sgh\-|shar|sie(\-|m)|sk\-0|sl(45|id)|sm(al|ar|b3|it|t5)|so(ft|ny)|sp(01|h\-|v\-|v )|sy(01|mb)|t2(18|50)|t6(00|10|18)|ta(gt|lk)|tcl\-|tdg\-|tel(i|m)|tim\-|t\-mo|to(pl|sh)|ts(70|m\-|m3|m5)|tx\-9|up(\.b|g1|si)|utst|v400|v750|veri|vi(rg|te)|vk(40|5[0-3]|\-v)|vm40|voda|vulc|vx(52|53|60|61|70|80|81|83|85|98)|w3c(\-| )|webc|whit|wi(g |nc|nw)|wmlb|wonu|x700|yas\-|your|zeto|zte\-/i.test(a.substr(0,4))) check = true;})(navigator.userAgent||navigator.vendor||window.opera);
              return check;
        };

    var _isMobile = window.mobilecheck();
    if (_isMobile) {
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').addClass('mobile');
    }

    var emailValid = "",
        time = 3000,
        btnStatus = true,
        errorStatus = false,
        errormessage = "<p class='gdpr_err'><b>Please Enter a valid email address<b><p>";

    function init() {
        setTimeout(function() {
            var cookieExist = getCookie("gdpr");
            if (cookieExist) {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie exist");
                return false;
            } else {
                //console.log("gdpr cookie does not exist")
                gdprMessage();
            }
            //Events
            $('#closebtn').on("click", hideForm);

            //Handle submit
            $('#gdpr-message-btn').on("click", function(event) {
                handleClick();
            });

            // //Hide if clicked outside div - TO DO stop handling click after submit
            // $(document).click(function(event) {
            // 	event.stopPropagation();
            //   console.log(event.target);
            //   if (!$(event.target).closest("#gdpr-message-content").length) {
            //     $("body").find("#gdpr-message-modal").hide();
            //     $(this).off();
            //   }
            // });
            $('#gdpr-con-btn').click(function() {
                setCookie("gdpr", "true");
                hideForm();
            });
        }, time);
    }

    //Show the message
    function gdprMessage() {
        //console.log("Show GDPR Message");
        var tMessage, emailInput, messageButton, ewrap;

        $('#gdpr-message-modal').show();
    }

    function handleClick() {
        //console.log($("#gdpr-input").val());
        emailValid = validateEmail($("#gdpr-input").val());
        if (emailValid) {
            //Submit the form
            //Hide form
            if ($('.gdpr_err')) {
                $('.gdpr_err').hide();
            }

            $("#gdpr-message-content")
                //If successful then...
            setCookie("gdpr", "true");
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid + " submiting form");
        } else {
            //Show error message
            gdprErrorMessage();
            //console.log("emailValid " + emailValid);
        }
    }

    function gdprErrorMessage() {
        if (errorStatus) {
            return false;
        } else {
            errorStatus = true;
            $("#gdpr-message-content").append(errormessage);
        }
    }

    function validateEmail(email) {
        var re = /^(([^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+(\.[^<>()\[\]\\.,;:\s@"]+)*)|(".+"))@((\[[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\.[0-9]{1,3}\])|(([a-zA-Z\-0-9]+\.)+[a-zA-Z]{2,}))$/;
        return re.test(String(email).toLowerCase());
    }

    function setCookie(name, value) {
        var expires = "";
        expires = "; expires=Fri, 31 Dec 9999 23:59:59 GMT";
        document.cookie = name + "=" + (value || "") + expires + "; path=/";
    }

    function getCookie(name) {
        var match = document.cookie.match(new RegExp(name + '=([^;]+)'));
        if (match) return match[1];
    }

    function hideForm() { //And set cookie
        $('#gdpr-message-modal').hide();
        setCookie("gdpr", "false");
        gtag('event', 'GDPR Modal', { 'event_category': 'Pubs GDPR', 'event_label':'GDPR Dismissal'});
    }

    return {
        init: init
    }
})();

$(document).ready(infoCentralCapture.init);
</script>


                    
                        



        
        <script nonce="90da8e4f5d2cb325-SJC">
var currentJournal = "ACS Applied Materials &amp;amp; Interfaces";
$(".citationLinks > a").click(function(e){
    if($(this).text() === "ACS Full Text ") {
        gtag('event', 'ACS Full Text', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Crossref") {
        gtag('event', 'Crossref', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "CAS") {
        gtag('event', 'CAS', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "PubMed") {
        gtag('event', 'PubMed', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).text() === "Google Scholar") {
        gtag('event', 'Google Scholar', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
    else if($(this).hasClass("issue-item_open-url") === true) {
        gtag('event', 'OpenURL', { 'event_category': 'Reference _Click', 'event_label':currentJournal});
    }
});
</script>
